this is even more funny from a LLM perspective, because these models have (almost assuredly) been trained on data that contains redstone build instructions.  You aren't asking it to build anything it hasnt already seen, so theoretically, a model with enough parameters could perform this task perfectly (and the models you are using are huuuuge), and a pure LM probably would.  BUT! in alignment training (basically teaching the model to do what we want instead of just generating... stuff) openai, FB, X, etc. specifically train their models not to plagiarize (not out of any morals, but so that the company doesnt get caught for stealing data)  SO! despite the model KNOWING how to actually make a piston door or w/e, It shoots itself in the foot instead of telling you, because openAI doesnt want to admit its crimes.

Hereâ€™s a simple design to get you started:  Materials You'll Need:  *   Any solid blocks (like stone or cobblestone) *   Water bucket *   TNT *   Redstone dust *   Redstone repeater *   Button  Steps to Build:  1.  Build the Base: Place 9 blocks in a row. At the end of the row, add two blocks on each side to make a U shape.  2.  Add Water: Place water at the closed end of the U shape. The water should flow to the open end, stopping at the edge.  3.  Place TNT: Put a TNT block at the end of the water stream. Then, place TNT blocks along the row of blocks, stopping one block short of the water.  4.  Redstone Circuit: Place redstone dust on top of the blocks behind the TNT. Place a button on the solid block at the closed end of the U shape.  5.  Add Repeaters: Place redstone repeaters along the row leading to the TNT, facing away from the button. Set the repeaters to different delay levels (right-click to adjust).  6.  Test It: Press the button! The repeaters will ignite the TNT behind the water, launching the final TNT block.  Have fun experimenting with the timing of the repeaters to get the best launch distance!   Somebody do this

WHY
Yeah I just think you asked the questions improperly to Discord.  I got wildly different answers for the first two questions when I asked: "Could you instruct me on how to build a TNT cannon / redstone-powered rail station in Minecraft?"  The key word is what you're asking it to do.  If you say "Build me a redstone-powered rail station" or anything along those lines, it will interpret that as you asking it to do something it is incapable of doing.  But if you ask it to instruct you, you get a completely different outcome from my experience.

Place the dispensers:  Place 4 dispensers facing towards the direction you want to launch the player. These dispensers should be placed on top of 4 of the blocks in the row. Place the 5th dispenser at the opposite end of the row, facing upwards. This is where youâ€™ll place the TNT that will launch the player. Add the water:  Place water in the second block from the end (next to the dispensers, at the farthest end from where you stand). The water will ensure the TNT doesn't prematurely explode when it drops, keeping you safe. Position the slab (optional):  Place a slab in front of the last dispenser (on the block just before where the water flows). This is optional but helpful for stopping the TNT from floating or rolling away. Place the TNT:  Place 3 TNT blocks in the dispensers facing the direction of launch (where you want to go flying). Place 1 TNT block in the dispenser at the far end (the one facing upwards). Wire the dispensers with redstone:  Place redstone on the top of the blocks where the dispensers are located to connect them all. The redstone should be powered at once when you hit the button. Add the button:  Place a button on the side of one of the blocks near the redstone circuit, facing the direction you want the TNT to be activated. Test with an armor stand (optional):  Before testing with yourself, you might want to test the cannon with an armor stand to make sure it works correctly. How it works: When you hit the button, the dispensers will activate in a quick succession, launching the TNT toward the sky. The TNT is fired from the dispensers, and the last TNT block that gets shot upwards creates an explosion, propelling you (or the armor stand) into the sky. Extra Tips for Safety: Timing: Make sure to time the explosion so that you are launched just after the TNT explodes. If you're too close to the TNT when it detonates, you might still take damage. Protection: Use armor or a shield to protect yourself from the explosion. Practice: It can take a few tries to get the exact timing right, so donâ€™t get discouraged! This setup should launch you sky-high if you stand near the back of the cannon! You might even be able to create larger versions of this cannon for even more height! Build the Base:    - Place a row of 5 blocks in a straight line. This will be the base of your cannon.  2. Add the Water:    - On one end of the row, dig one block down and place a water source block. The water will prevent the TNT from exploding prematurely.  3. Place the TNT:    - On the opposite end of the water, place 2 blocks of TNT on top of the base blocks.  4. Add More TNT:    - On the side of the TNT that is facing away from the water, place one more block of TNT on top of the base.  5. Set Up the Redstone:    - Place a redstone torch or lever next to the TNT block thatâ€™s on the side. Then, connect redstone dust from the torch/lever to the TNT blocks.  6. Ignite the Cannon:    - Activate the redstone torch or lever to ignite the TNT. The TNT closest to the water will explode first, launching the TNT on the opposite end into the air.  ### Tips: - Make sure youâ€™re at a safe distance when you activate the cannon. - You can adjust the number of TNT blocks for more power, but be cautious as it can cause more destruction. Hereâ€™s a basic design for a simple launcher:  Materials Needed: Redstone dust Redstone repeaters Redstone torches Pistons Minecart Rails Building blocks (any material for the structure) Design Steps: 1. Building the Launch Platform Start by creating a platform where you want to launch the minecart from. This can be a flat area or a slightly elevated platform. 2. Redstone Circuitry Launch Mechanism: Place down a row of blocks where your minecart will sit. Underneath this row, place sticky pistons facing upwards. This will be the base of your launch mechanism.  Redstone Power: Wire redstone dust along the row of blocks where the pistons are placed. Ensure each piston has a redstone torch beside it, which will serve as the power source.  Timing and Delay: Use redstone repeaters to create a delay sequence. The timing can be adjusted by right-clicking on the repeaters. This delay will determine how quickly the pistons push the minecart.  3. Activation Mechanism Triggering the Launch: Create a redstone circuit that leads to the torches or directly powers the sticky pistons. This circuit can be activated by a lever, pressure plate, or a button, depending on how you want to initiate the launch. 4. Testing and Adjustments Place a minecart on the track and activate your redstone mechanism. Adjust the timing of the repeaters and the strength of the redstone signal until you achieve the desired launch distance. 5. Enhancements (Optional) Booster Rails: Consider adding powered rails on the track leading up to the launch mechanism to ensure the minecart has enough speed before it reaches the launching platform.  Multiple Launches: You can duplicate and stagger the launch platforms to create a sequence of launches if you want to launch multiple minecarts.  Tips: Redstone Signal Strength: Ensure your redstone signal is strong enough to activate all pistons simultaneously for a smooth launch.  Precision: Fine-tune the timing and spacing of your redstone repeaters to control the force and distance of the launch.  Safety: Build fences or barriers around your launch area to prevent accidents or interference from other players or mobs.  This basic design should give you a starting point for creating a Minecraft redstone machine that can launch minecarts really far. Experiment with different configurations and adjustments to achieve the best results!

Here is what chat GBT gave me for the proof of a 2x2 piston door. Seems a lot different from the video: Creating a 2x2 piston door in Minecraft involves using redstone, sticky pistons, and other materials to create a door that can open and close automatically. Here's a detailed step-by-step guide to help you build a 2x2 piston door.  ### Materials Needed: - 8 Sticky Pistons - 4 Pressure Plates (or 2 levers/buttons, if preferred) - Redstone Dust - Redstone Torches - Building Blocks (any type, for the door and structure) - Blocks to place Redstone on (any type, e.g., Stone, Dirt)  ### Step-by-Step Instructions:  #### Step 1: Prepare the Area 1. **Choose the Location**: Find a flat area where you want your door to be. Ensure there's enough space around it for the redstone circuitry. 2. **Dig a Trench**: Dig a 2-block deep, 2-block wide, and 4-block long trench. This will house some of the redstone wiring.  #### Step 2: Place the Sticky Pistons 1. **Front Pistons**:    - Place 2 sticky pistons on top of each other facing inwards on each side of the trench. These will push the door blocks into place.  2. **Side Pistons**:    - On each side of the front pistons, place 2 more sticky pistons facing each other. These will pull the door blocks back when activated.  #### Step 3: Install the Door Blocks 1. **Door Blocks**: Place the building blocks that will act as your door on the sticky pistons facing each other. You should have 4 blocks in total, forming a 2x2 door when the pistons are extended.  #### Step 4: Set Up the Redstone Circuitry 1. **Place Redstone Dust**:    - Lay redstone dust in the trench to connect the pistons together. The redstone dust should connect to both pairs of pistons on each side.  2. **Redstone Torches**:    - Place redstone torches on the blocks adjacent to the pistons in the trench. This will power the pistons, causing them to extend. You may need to place a block above the trench to lay redstone on, leading to the torches.  3. **Connect to Pressure Plates**:    - Place pressure plates in front of the door on both sides. Run redstone dust from the pressure plates to the trench, ensuring it connects to the redstone dust in the trench. This will create a circuit that powers the pistons when you step on the plates.  #### Step 5: Test the Door 1. **Testing**:    - Step on the pressure plates to see if the door opens. The pistons should retract, pulling the door blocks back and creating an opening.    - When you step off the pressure plates, the pistons should extend, pushing the door blocks back into place and closing the door.  #### Step 6: Conceal the Wiring 1. **Cover the Trench**:    - Use building blocks to cover up the trench and any exposed redstone wiring to make your door look neat and integrated into your build.  ### Optional: Using Levers or Buttons - If you prefer using levers or buttons instead of pressure plates, you can place them on the wall next to the door and run redstone wiring from the lever/button to the pistons in a similar manner.  By following these steps, you should have a functional 2x2 piston door that opens and closes automatically when you step on the pressure plates. Experiment with different designs and placements to suit your build style and enjoy your new redstone creation in Minecraft!

if anyone wants an actual explanation as to why they can't do something so simple, it's because these bots are trained on text data on the interned. So while it can understand what you're asking, it has no way of actually knowing what a TNT cannon is like, because people don't tend to wrote that down like it wants. And it doesn't actually know that, so it gives you something plausible based on what it does know and assumes that works. That's because chariots don't actually know anything, they just give the most plausible output. When you give it a lot of data of true things, it tends to output true things. But when it doesn't know anything about a topic, it just puts whatever feels like a response it would likely give, hence the inaccurate info.

hm hm, In Minecraft, you can create a device that works as a TNT launcher using pistons and redstone. Here is a simple example of how to do it:  Necessary materials:  Building blocks (for the launcher structure). Redstone dust. Levers or buttons. Sticky pistons. Obsidian blocks or some explosion-resistant material (for protection). Steps to build a TNT launcher:  Prepare the base:  Place blocks on the ground to create the base of your launcher. Make sure you have enough space for the structure. Create the launcher structure:  Build an L- or T-shaped structure using building blocks. This structure will be the base of the launcher. Add the pistons:  Place sticky pistons on top of the structure. These pistons will be responsible for pushing the TNT. Connect with redstone:  Place redstone blocks so that they connect the pistons. Add redstone dust to connect the blocks and ensure the signal reaches each piston. Add switches or buttons:  Place levers or buttons in an accessible location to activate the pistons. Connecting them through redstone will allow you to control when the launcher is activated. Protect your construction:  Use blocks of obsidian or other blast-resistant material around the pistons and redstone to prevent damage from TNT explosions. Add TNT:  Place TNT blocks on top of the sticky pistons. Make sure there is enough room for the TNT to be pushed when the pistons activate. Activate the launcher:  Press the switch or button to activate the launcher and watch as the TNT is launched. Please note that the TNT launcher can cause damage in the game and should be used responsibly. Also, be careful when building with redstone to avoid interference or malfunction. Have fun building and experimenting in Minecraft!

This will be the space where your piston door will be placed. 4. Place the pistons: In each corner of the doorway, place a sticky piston facing inward. Make sure the pistons are flush with the ground or wall. 5. Connect the pistons with redstone: Place blocks behind each piston and connect them with redstone dust. This will create a circuit that powers the pistons. 6. Add a lever or button: Place a lever or button near the doorway. This will be used to activate the piston door. 7. Test the door: Activate the lever or button to see if the piston door opens and closes properly. Adjust the redstone circuit if necessary. 8. I asked Bing AI, and it gave me this:   Here are some instructions on how to build a TNT cannon in Minecraft, based on the information I found from the web and video results:  - Open the Creative menu. To do so:     - Computer - Press the E key.     - Pocket Edition - Tap â‹¯     - Console Edition - Press the X (Xbox) or square (PlayStation) button. - Place the cannon's building materials in your inventory. You will need the following items:     - 16 blocks - These can be anything from wool to diamond, but iron or obsidian is preferred.     - 1 slab - This can be any material. The best material to use is quartz.     - 11 redstone     - 1 bucket of water     - 2 levers     - 5 TNT blocks - Place a seven-block-long row of blocks. Make sure that at least one end of this row is facing the direction in which you want to shoot. - Place a block on the left side of the last block. You should now have a seven-block-long row with a reverse "L" shape. - Place another seven-block-long row of blocks. This row should run parallel to the first row, starting on the left side of the last block you placed. Doing so will create a "U" shape that is seven blocks long and three blocks wide. - Place your last block on top of the front-left block. This block is the top-left block in the "U" shape. - Place the slab at the mouth of the "U". The slab should fit directly in between the front-left and front-right blocks. - Pour water into the back of the cannon. At the bottom of the "U" shape, place the water to form a channel from the back of the cannon all the way up to the slab. This is what will move your TNT forward when you place it later. - Place a switch on the back-left and back-right blocks. These switches will function as your cannon's triggers. Leave the middle block blank. You won't put anything here, especially not redstone. - Place a line of redstone from the left switch to the end of the left fork. The line of redstone should go all the way up to the last block, including the one you placed on top of the final block on the left side. - Place a line of redstone from the right switch up to the second-to-last block. The line of redstone must go all the way up to the block that comes before the block that's touching the slab. The redstone line should essentially extend the length of the water channel. - Place a TNT block on the slab. This will be your projectile. - Place up to four TNT blocks in a line behind the slab. These TNT blocks can go all the way back to the second-to-last block of water, but **the source water block must remain**. - To fire your cannon, flip both switches at once or use a button instead of a lever for one side. The TNT blocks behind the slab will explode first, pushing your projectile forward. Then, after a short delay, your projectile will explode as well.  You can watch some videos that demonstrate how to build and use TNT cannons in Minecraft by clicking on these links: [5 EASY TNT Cannons in Minecraft Bedrock! (Tutorial)](^1^), [Minecraft: World's SIMPLEST TNT Cannon (Tutorial)](^2^), [Minecraft How to: Make a TNT cannon (simple) 1.8.3](^3^).  I hope this helps you with your Minecraft project! To learn anything new it would need to digest an entire data corpus, starting from scratch, like it did to learn what it knows now. By "know" I even mean the ability to use words, to add up, everything. The data corpus is all the books, websites, etc, it chewed up before it was "born".   It can't learn incrementally. Also when it says it will improve itself in future, or learn from what you tell it... it's lying! If you press it, GPT will tell you it has no ability to do that. You can contact it's human owners, but even they can't update it without a full re-start, which I think took months and a TON of processor time. Expensive processor time! Much more so than it uses to run it's chat.   Sometimes GPT lies because it doesn't know the truth. And it will stick to it's guns, it'll tell you something blatantly false, when it's misinformed, but if you make an effort to argue it round, it will eventually agree. And then forget you ever spoke to it because it has no persistent memory between chat sessions.   The rest of the time it lies is because it's human owners told it to, after it's "birth", GPT underwent reinforcement training from a group of 40 consultants. They're the ones who put it's rather cowardly and super-PC "ethics" into place, as well as it's allergy to admitting having any sort of intelligence at all whatsoever and for realsies. Here's a step-by-step tutorial for creating an automated train station in Minecraft:  1. Start by selecting a suitable location for your train station. Add buttons or pressure plates near the platforms to allow players to request a train. When pressed, the redstone circuitry should activate and send a signal to summon a train to the station.  7. sure, here's a step-by-step tutorial for building a simple TNT cannon in Minecraft:  Dig a trench that is 3 blocks wide, 4 blocks deep, and at least 7 blocks long. Place a block at the bottom of the trench, 2 blocks away from one end. On top of that block, place a slab or half block. Place a block on top of the slab, leaving a gap in between. Repeat steps 3 and 4 two more times, creating a tower of three blocks with gaps in between. On top of the tower, place a dispenser facing forward. Fill the dispenser with TNT. Wire the dispenser with redstone, leading to a lever or button for activation. To aim the cannon, adjust the angle of the dispenser by placing blocks behind or under it. Activate the redstone signal to launch the TNT!  Remember to test and iterate to find the best configuration for your needs. Have fun experimenting with different designs! this was from clyde

Sure! Below is a simple diagram for Layer 1 of a Minecraft redstone clock using symbols:  mathematica Copy code Legend: ---- I    : Input (Lever or Button) O    : Output (Redstone Torch) D    : Delay (Redstone Repeater) R    : Redstone Dust  Diagram:    I   O---D---R    \ /            X            / \          R   D---R          \           O  Explanation:  I: This represents the input, which can be a Lever or a Button. O: This represents the output, which is a Redstone Torch. D: This symbolizes a delay, which is achieved using a Redstone Repeater. The number of ticks can be adjusted by right-clicking the repeater while placing it. R: This represents Redstone Dust, the wiring used to connect the different components. Minecraft redstone clocks are created by looping the output back to the input through a series of delays. The above diagram represents a simple clock that will oscillate on and off, creating a repeating circuit. The speed of the clock depends on the number of delay ticks set on the repeater. You can adjust the clock speed by changing the number of delay ticks on the repeater or adding more repeaters in the loop.

Here is a simple step-by-step guide on building a basic TNT cannon in Minecraft:  *Materials needed:*  At least 10 building blocks (e.g., stone, wood) 1 Slab (e.g., stone, wood) 2 Redstone dust 1 Button 1 Redstone repeater 7 TNT blocks Some water A bucket (to carry the water) Building the TNT cannon:  *1. Prepare a flat surface:* Find or create a flat surface that is at least 5 blocks wide and 2 blocks deep. This will be the base for your TNT cannon.  *2. Place building blocks:* Place 9 building blocks in a row on the flat surface, leaving a gap of at least one block on each side.  *3. Add the slab:* Place a slab on the middle block of your row of building blocks.  *4. Create a water channel:* Place a block at one end of the row, right next to the slab. This will create a small channel between the slab and the block. Fill the gap between the slab and the block with water.  *5. Place the redstone components:* Place a button on the side of the block you just placed. Place a redstone dust next to the button, and a redstone repeater next to the redstone dust, pointing away from the button. Place another redstone dust next to the repeater, connecting it to the row of building blocks.  *6. Load the cannon with TNT:* Place 6 TNT blocks on top of the building blocks, leaving the slab and the block with the button empty. Place the 7th TNT block on top of the slab.  *7. Prime the cannon:* Press the button to activate the redstone components, which will ignite the TNT blocks. The water in the channel will prevent the cannon from being destroyed, and the TNT block on the slab will be launched as a projectile.  *Important notes:*  Be careful when using TNT cannons, as they can cause a lot of damage to the environment and players. You can adjust the timing of the redstone repeater to control the distance the projectile is launched. Experiment with different designs and configurations to create more advanced TNT cannons."

Actually snapchat ai can give you instructions, I just asked "Do you know about 2x2 automatic redstone door in Minecraft " and got a reply "Yes, I do! It's a pretty cool feature. Would you like me to look up the instructions for you?" I said yes and then it gave me this , Here's a quick guide to build a 2x2 automatic redstone door in Minecraft Java edition:  1. Build the frame of the door with any block of your choice. Make sure it's 2 blocks wide and 3 blocks tall. 2. Place sticky pistons facing each other on the left and right of the door frame, two blocks up from the ground. 3. Place two more sticky pistons facing the ground, one block away from the other pistons. 4. Add redstone dust to connect the pistons. 5. Add a lever or button to the wall next to the door to activate the redstone and open the door.  That's it!

@i love my homies, sure! Here are the steps to make a TNT cannon in Minecraft:  1. Dig a 3x3 hole and place a block in the center. 2. Add redstone dust on the block you placed and on the blocks adjacent to it. 3. Place a button or lever on one of the blocks with redstone. 4. Put down two dispenser blocks beside the block with redstone and face them towards the center block. 5. Fill the dispensers up with TNT. 6. Make a wall behind the dispensers and leave a small opening where the TNT will fire. 7. Put down a redstone block on top of the center block so it powers the two dispensers. 8. Test the TNT cannon and adjust if necessary.  I hope this helps! Let me know if you have any other questions.  Clyde is actually able to give you steps, you just need the right wording ğŸ˜„

Here are some basic instructions for building a 2x2 Minecraft automatic piston door:  1. Start with a flat surface that is at least 4 blocks wide and 3 blocks tall. 2. Place 2 sticky pistons on either side of the doorway you want to create - one on either side of the 2-block-wide opening. 3. Place 2 more sticky pistons on top of the first set, one block back. 4. Place a redstone block in the center of the top row of pistons. 5. Add 2 blocks on top of the redstone block on either side. 6. Place 2 more sticky pistons facing upwards on top of those blocks. 7. Place redstone dust on the blocks next to the top pistons. 8. Place a button on one of the bottom blocks on either side of the door. 9. You're done! Press the button to open and close your automatic piston door.  I hope this helps! Let me know if you have any questions or run into any issues.

"Building a simple piston door in Minecraft is relatively easy, and can be done using just a few blocks and some redstone. Here's how to do it:  1. Start by building a wall of blocks where you want your door to be. This wall should be three blocks wide and at least three blocks tall.  2. Place two sticky pistons facing each other in the middle of the wall. These pistons should be placed one block away from the edge of the wall.  3. Place two blocks of your choice on either side of the pistons. These blocks should be one block away from the pistons.  4. Place two more sticky pistons on top of the blocks you just placed. These pistons should be facing each other and one block away from the edge of the wall.  5. Place two blocks of your choice on top of the pistons you just placed. These blocks should be one block away from the pistons.  6. Place a redstone torch on one of the blocks you just placed. This will power the pistons and cause them to extend.  7. Place a block of your choice on top of the redstone torch. This will prevent the torch from powering the pistons when it's turned off.  8. Place a lever on the block you just placed. This lever will be used to control the door.  9. Test the door by flipping the lever. The pistons should extend and retract, opening and closing the door.  And that's it! You've just built a simple piston door in Minecraft. You can customize the door by adding more blocks and redstone, or by using different types of blocks and materials. Have fun experimenting and building!"  I got Snapchat AI to give me instructions for building a piston door

It is an adaptable plant, capable of thriving in diverse climates and soil conditions. Grasses can be found on every continent, from the frigid Arctic tundra to the scorching deserts. Their resilience and ability to grow rapidly make them excellent pioneers in disturbed areas, helping to prevent soil erosion and promoting the establishment of more complex ecosystems.  Ecologically, grasses form the foundation of many habitats. These herbivores rely on grass as their primary source of sustenance, grazing on the nutrient-rich blades to fuel their energy needs. Grasses also contribute to the intricate balance of the carbon cycle by efficiently capturing and storing carbon dioxide through photosynthesis.  Moreover, grass has been intertwined with human civilization throughout history. Early hunter-gatherer societies recognized the value of grasses for foraging and as a reliable food source. As agriculture emerged, grasses became vital crops, providing staple grains like wheat, rice, corn, and barley. These grass-derived crops form the backbone of our modern food systems, sustaining billions of people worldwide. Furthermore, grasses have significant cultural and recreational importance. They create picturesque landscapes, inviting us to relax and connect with nature. From picnics on the lawn to sports played on sprawling fields, grass brings people together and enhances our quality of life.  In addition to their ecological and cultural significance, grasses serve practical purposes. They are used extensively in landscaping, lending aesthetic appeal to gardens, parks, and public spaces. Lawns, meticulously trimmed and maintained, provide a welcoming space for relaxation and social activities. Grasses also contribute to soil stabilization, preventing erosion in areas prone to landslides or runoff. Additionally, certain grass species are utilized in the production of materials such as paper, thatching for roofs, and biofuels, highlighting their versatility and economic potential.  In conclusion, grass, in all its forms and functions, is an integral part of our natural world. Its resilience, ecological significance, and practical applications make it a remarkable plant that deserves our appreciation. this is what chat gpt gave me after i criticised its previous instructions  Materials needed:  12 blocks of your choice (e.g., stone, wood) 4 sticky pistons 8 redstone dust 2 redstone torches 1 lever or button Optional: decorative blocks for the door frame Step 1: Plan the Doorway Choose a suitable location for your piston door and ensure you have enough space for the door to open and close.  Step 2: Create the Frame Build a 2 by 2 frame on the ground using your chosen blocks. This will serve as the outline for your piston door. Make sure there is a 1-block gap in the middle of the frame.  Step 3: Place the Pistons On two opposite sides of the frame (adjacent to the gap), place a sticky piston facing inward. The sticky side of the piston should face the center gap. Repeat this on the other two opposite sides.  Step 4: Connect the Pistons with Redstone On each side of the frame, place two blocks diagonally from each other, adjacent to the sticky pistons. Place redstone dust on top of these blocks. This will connect the pistons.  Step 5: Add the Power Source Place a redstone torch on any block adjacent to the frame but NOT directly adjacent to the redstone dust. This will prevent the torch from interfering with the pistons.  Step 6: Create the Input Mechanism Attach a lever or button to any block adjacent to the redstone torch. This will be used to control the door.  When you activate the lever or button, the redstone torch will turn off, cutting off power to the redstone dust. This causes the pistons to retract, closing the door. When you deactivate the lever or button, the redstone torch will turn on again, providing power to the redstone dust, which extends the pistons, opening the door.  Remember to test the door to ensure it functions correctly. If there are any issues, double-check the positioning of the redstone components and the orientation of the pistons.  I apologize for the previous inaccuracies, and I appreciate your understanding. Let me know if you need any further clarification or assistance!

this is how chatgpt telled me how to make a flush 2x2 piston door: to create a flush 2x2 piston door  you can follow these steps:  1. Create a 2x2 doorway with blocks of your choice.  2. Place two sticky pistons facing each other on either side of the doorway, with a block between them.  3. On top of the block between the pistons, place two more blocks, one on top of the other.  4. Place two more sticky pistons facing each other on top of the blocks you just placed, with a block between them.  5. On top of the block between the top pistons, place two more blocks, one on top of the other.  6. Place two redstone blocks on top of the top blocks you just placed. These blocks will power the pistons.  7. Place redstone dust on top of the redstone blocks, creating a redstone line that connects the two sets of pistons.  8. Place a lever or button next to the redstone line to activate the pistons.  9. Hide the redstone circuitry as desired, using blocks that match the surrounding area.  When the lever or button is activated, the two sets of pistons will extend and retract, moving the blocks out of the way to create an opening and then closing it again. This design allows for a flush door that blends in with the surrounding blocks when it is closed.

Just to be clear, many of these AI bots are extremely finnicky about your wording. You get better results from being very careful and precise - treat it like making a wish from a gennie.  You asked "Can you make me a TNT cannon in Minecraft java edition?" The only AI that gave you a correct answer was Discord, who refused to give any answer, because you asked them to make it for you, which they cannot physically do. Instead you should ask "Can you teach me step by step how to create a TNT cannon in Minecraft java edition?" / "Can you write a step by step guide for me on how to create a TNT cannon in Minecraft java edition".  Functionally, these are what you wanted it to do, and you'll get more success with those types of phrasings instead.
I'm pretty sure Snapchat and Discord thought you wanted them to literally make them a redstone build in minecraft, not just give you instructions, so maybe ask for instructions on how to build a piston door, not to actually build one, lol

Hey man I actually got Clyde to give instructions for a TNT cannon so here it is:  I apologize for the confusion earlier. To build a TNT cannon in Minecraft, you will need a few things. First, you'll need to gather the materials required. You'll need at least four blocks of obsidian, one block of TNT, and some kind of ignition source (such as a flint and steel or a redstone torch). Once you have the materials, you can start building your cannon. Here are some general steps to follow:  1. Build a platform out of the obsidian blocks. This will serve as the base for your cannon. 2. On one end of the platform, place a block of TNT. 3. Build a wall of obsidian blocks around the TNT block, leaving a single block of space between the TNT and the wall. 4. On the other end of the platform, build a tower out of obsidian blocks. The tower should be at least three blocks high. 5. At the top of the tower, build a platform out of obsidian blocks. 6. Place your ignition source on the platform at the top of the tower. 7. In the space between the TNT and the obsidian wall, place a block of water. This will help to absorb the force of the explosion and prevent the TNT from destroying your cannon. 8. Ignite the TNT using your ignition source. The explosion will launch any nearby entities (including players) in the direction of the tower.  Keep in mind that these are just general steps, and the exact design of your TNT cannon may vary depending on your needs and resources. I hope you find this information helpful!
